# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Streams DSL to Processor API Migration

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Kafka Streams DSL (map, filter, groupBy) and their corresponding Processor API equivalents, to support a team migrating from DSL to lower-level Processor API for custom state store management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kafka Streams DSL to Processor API migration patterns in apache/kafka. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary

I've created a detailed JSON file (`/workspace/answer.json`) documenting:

### **Files Identified** (27 files)
- **DSL Interfaces**: KStream.java, KTable.java, KGroupedStream.java
- **DSL Implementations**: KStreamImpl.java, KTableImpl.java 
- **Processor API Adapters**: KStreamMap, KStreamFilter, KStreamFlatMap, KStreamMapValues, KStreamFlatMapValues, KStreamPeek, KStreamPrint, ForeachProcessor, PassThrough, KStreamBranch, KStreamAggregate, KStreamReduce, KTableAggregate, KTableFilter, KTableMapValues
- **Processor API Interfaces**: Processor, FixedKeyProcessor, ProcessorSupplier, FixedKeyProcessorSupplier, ProcessorContext, FixedKeyProcessorContext, Record, FixedKeyRecord

### **Key Operations & Implementations**
1. **filter** → KStreamFilter (FixedKeyProcessorSupplier)
2. **map** → KStreamMap (ProcessorSupplier)
3. **groupBy** → Uses KStreamMap internally for key selection
4. **flatMap** → KStreamFlatMap (ProcessorSupplier)
5. **mapValues** → KStreamMapValues (FixedKeyProcessorSupplier)
6. **flatMapValues** → KStreamFlatMapValues (FixedKeyProcessorSupplier)
7. **peek** → KStreamPeek (FixedKeyProcessorSupplier)
8. **foreach** → ForeachProcessor

### **Architecture Pattern**
Each DSL operation follows a consistent pattern:
- Public DSL method → Implementation class → ProcessorSupplier/FixedKeyProcessorSupplier adapter → Processor/FixedKeyProcessor implementation → context().forward()

The answer file includes execution chains showing how operations flow from DSL through to the Processor API, making it easy for teams to understand and implement custom processors with state store access.

Filter Operation**\\n- **DSL Interface**: `KStream.filter(Predicate<K, V>)` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/KStream.java:76)\\n- **DSL Implementation**: `KStreamImpl.filter()` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/internals/KStreamImpl.java:146-172)\\n- **Processor API Adapter**: `KStreamFilter<K, V>` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/internals/KStreamFilter.java:25)\\n- **Processor API Interface Used**: `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier<K, V, V>` which produces `FixedKeyProcessor<K, V, V>`\\n- **Implementation Detail**: KStreamFilter extends `ContextualFixedKeyProcessor` and uses the `FixedKeyRecord` type with forward() method to pass through filtered records\\n\\n**2. FlatMap Operation**\\n- **DSL Interface**: `KStream.flatMap(KeyValueMapper<K, V, Iterable<KeyValue<K', V'>>>)` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/KStream.java:306)\\n- **DSL Implementation**: `KStreamImpl.flatMap()` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/internals/KStreamImpl.java:314-335)\\n- **Processor API Adapter**: `KStreamFlatMap<KIn, VIn, KOut, VOut>` (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/internals/KStreamFlatMap.java:28)\\n- **Processor API Interface Used**: `ProcessorSupplier<KIn, VIn, KOut, VOut>` which produces `Processor<KIn, VIn, KOut, VOut>`\\n- **Implementation Detail**: KStreamFlatMap extends `ContextualProcessor` and forwards multiple records per input record using forward() in a loop\\n\\n**5. Processor Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/Processor.java:34)\\n- Generic interface with type parameters: `<KIn, VIn, KOut, VOut>`\\n- Allows transformation of both keys and values\\n- Methods: `init(ProcessorContext)`, `process(Record)`, `close()`\\n- Used for key-changing operations (map, flatMap)\\n\\n**2. FixedKeyProcessor Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/FixedKeyProcessor.java:33)\\n- Generic interface with type parameters: `<KIn, VIn, VOut>`\\n- Restricts key transformation; output keys match input keys\\n- Methods: `init(FixedKeyProcessorContext)`, `process(FixedKeyRecord)`, `close()`\\n- Used for value-only transformations (filter, mapValues, flatMapValues, peek)\\n\\n**3. ProcessorSupplier Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/ProcessorSupplier.java)\\n- Factory pattern interface for creating Processor instances\\n- Allows custom initialization and reuse of Processor objects\\n- Returns new Processor instances via `get()` method\\n\\n**4. FixedKeyProcessorSupplier Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/FixedKeyProcessorSupplier.java)\\n- Factory pattern interface for creating FixedKeyProcessor instances\\n- Similar to ProcessorSupplier but for FixedKeyProcessor\\n\\n### Bridge Mechanism: process() and processValues() Methods\\n\\nThe DSL provides explicit bridge methods to the Processor API:\\n\\n**process() Method** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/KStream.java:1550-1564)\\n- Accepts a `ProcessorSupplier<K, V, KOut, VOut>`\\n- Allows custom Processor implementation with full control\\n- Supports key-changing operations with potential repartitioning\\n- Use case: Custom state store management, complex transformations\\n\\n**processValues() Method** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/KStream.java:1580-1594)\\n- Accepts a `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier<K, V, VOut>`\\n- Restricts to FixedKeyProcessor, preserving key co-location\\n- No repartitioning needed; efficient for value-only operations\\n- Use case: Custom state store management without key changes\\n\\n### Architecture Pattern\\n\\nThe DSL-to-Processor API migration follows a consistent pattern:\\n\\n1. **DSL Method** (e.g., `KStream.map()`) defines the public API\\n2. **Implementation Class** (e.g., `KStreamImpl.map()`) orchestrates the operation\\n3. **Adapter Class** (e.g., `KStreamMap`) implements `ProcessorSupplier` or `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier`\\n4. **Processor Class** (inner class) extends `ContextualProcessor` or `ContextualFixedKeyProcessor` and implements `process(Record)`\\n5. **Context Usage** The processor uses `context().forward()` to emit records downstream\\n\\nThis design allows teams migrating to the Processor API to:\\n- Understand how DSL operations work internally\\n- Implement custom processors with state store access\\n- Maintain similar semantics to DSL operations\\n- Access ProcessorContext features (scheduling, punctuation, state stores)\\n\\n### Key Implementation Files for Migration Reference\\n\\n- **DSL Interfaces**: KStream.java, KTable.java define all high-level operations\\n- **DSL Implementations**: KStreamImpl.java orchestrates DSL operations\\n- **Adapter Classes**: KStreamMap.java, KStreamFilter.java, etc., show how to adapt DSL operations to Processor API\\n- **Processor API Core**: Processor.java, FixedKeyProcessor.java define the low-level abstraction\\n- **Context Interfaces**: ProcessorContext.java, FixedKeyProcessorContext.java provide state store and runtime access\\n- **Record Types**: Record.java, FixedKeyRecord.java define the data flow between processors\"\n}\n",

Processor Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/Processor.java:34)\\n- Generic interface with type parameters: `<KIn, VIn, KOut, VOut>`\\n- Allows transformation of both keys and values\\n- Methods: `init(ProcessorContext)`, `process(Record)`, `close()`\\n- Used for key-changing operations (map, flatMap)\\n\\n**2. FixedKeyProcessor Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/FixedKeyProcessor.java:33)\\n- Generic interface with type parameters: `<KIn, VIn, VOut>`\\n- Restricts key transformation; output keys match input keys\\n- Methods: `init(FixedKeyProcessorContext)`, `process(FixedKeyRecord)`, `close()`\\n- Used for value-only transformations (filter, mapValues, flatMapValues, peek)\\n\\n**3. ProcessorSupplier Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/ProcessorSupplier.java)\\n- Factory pattern interface for creating Processor instances\\n- Allows custom initialization and reuse of Processor objects\\n- Returns new Processor instances via `get()` method\\n\\n**4. FixedKeyProcessorSupplier Interface** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/processor/api/FixedKeyProcessorSupplier.java)\\n- Factory pattern interface for creating FixedKeyProcessor instances\\n- Similar to ProcessorSupplier but for FixedKeyProcessor\\n\\n### Bridge Mechanism: process() and processValues() Methods\\n\\nThe DSL provides explicit bridge methods to the Processor API:\\n\\n**process() Method** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/KStream.java:1550-1564)\\n- Accepts a `ProcessorSupplier<K, V, KOut, VOut>`\\n- Allows custom Processor implementation with full control\\n- Supports key-changing operations with potential repartitioning\\n- Use case: Custom state store management, complex transformations\\n\\n**processValues() Method** (streams/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/streams/kstream/KStream.java:1580-1594)\\n- Accepts a `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier<K, V, VOut>`\\n- Restricts to FixedKeyProcessor, preserving key co-location\\n- No repartitioning needed; efficient for value-only operations\\n- Use case: Custom state store management without key changes\\n\\n### Architecture Pattern\\n\\nThe DSL-to-Processor API migration follows a consistent pattern:\\n\\n1. **DSL Method** (e.g., `KStream.map()`) defines the public API\\n2. **Implementation Class** (e.g., `KStreamImpl.map()`) orchestrates the operation\\n3. **Adapter Class** (e.g., `KStreamMap`) implements `ProcessorSupplier` or `FixedKeyProcessorSupplier`\\n4. **Processor Class** (inner class) extends `ContextualProcessor` or `ContextualFixedKeyProcessor` and implements `process(Record)`\\n5. **Context Usage** The processor uses `context().forward()` to emit records downstream\\n\\nThis design allows teams migrating to the Processor API to:\\n- Understand how DSL operations work internally\\n- Implement custom processors with state store access\\n- Maintain similar semantics to DSL operations\\n- Access ProcessorContext features (scheduling, punctuation, state stores)\\n\\n### Key Implementation Files for Migration Reference\\n\\n- **DSL Interfaces**: KStream.java, KTable.java define all high-level operations\\n- **DSL Implementations**: KStreamImpl.java orchestrates DSL operations\\n- **Adapter Classes**: KStreamMap.java, KStreamFilter.java, etc., show how to adapt DSL operations to Processor API\\n- **Processor API Core**: Processor.java, FixedKeyProcessor.java define the low-level abstraction\\n- **Context Interfaces**: ProcessorContext.java, FixedKeyProcessorContext.java provide state store and runtime access\\n- **Record Types**: Record.java, FixedKeyRecord.java define the data flow between processors\"\n}\n",
